propagated by People&#8217;s Daily.</p> </span><div class="mvp-author-info-wrap left relative"><div class="mvp-author-info-thumb left relative"> <img Check it out: https://www.whatsonweibo.com/100-terms-communist-party-wants-know-19th-cpc-national-congress/"><li class="mvp-soc-mob-email"> <i class="fa fa-envelope-o" aria-hidden="true"></i></li> </a> <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/100-terms-communist-party-wants-know-19th-cpc-national-congress/#respond"><li class="mvp-soc-mob-com mvp-com-click"> <i class="fa fa-comment-o" aria-hidden="true"></i></li> </a></ul></div></div><div class="mvp-soc-mob-right left relative"> <i class="fa fa-ellipsis-h" aria-hidden="true"></i></div></div></div><div class="mvp-post-soc-in"><div id="mvp-content-body" class="left relative"><div id="mvp-content-body-top" class=left relative"><div id="mvp-content-main" class="left relative"><div id="tps_slideContainer_15287" class="theiaPostSlider_slides"><div class="theiaPostSlider_preloadedSlide"><p><span class="myintro">These are the 100 terms to know for the 19th CPC National Congress &#8211; propagated by <em>People&#8217;s Daily</em>, the mouthpiece of China&#8217;s ruling Communist Party, on Weibo.</span></p><p><span class="big">I</span>t is the week of the 19th National Congress of the Communist Party of China (CPC), better known as the &#8220;19th Party Congress.&#8221; This meeting, that takes place from October 18 to October 24, is a major event that takes place every five years.</p><p>On Chinese social media, Communist Party newspaper <em>People&#8217;s Daily</em> (@<a href="https://www.weibo.com/rmrb?refer_flag=1001030103_" target="_blank" rel="noopener">人民日报</a>) presented a vocabulary list for people to know before the huge political event.</p><p>During the 19th Party Congress approximately 2280 delegates from across the nation officially come together to select the party’s top leadership for the next five years. The event is <a href="http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/10/explained-national-congress-china-communist-party-171017140021234.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">also called</a> a &#8220;celebration of decisions that have already been taken,&#8221; as the key points of the meeting have mostly already been settled behind closed doors.</p><p>It is these key decisions for China that will be discussed during the CPC National Congress and then officially announced, representing &#8220;new governance concepts, thoughts and strategies proposed by the CPC Central Committee with Xi Jinping at its core&#8221; (<em><a href="http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-10/17/c_136686771.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Xinhua</a></em>).</p><p>In a recent report by <a href="http://www.apcoworldwide.com/blog/detail/apcoforum/2017/10/16/chinas-19th-party-congress" target="_blank" rel="noopener">APCO Worldwide</a>, Gary Li summarizes what to look out for during the 19th National Congress, writing that it is likely for President Xi Jinping to &#8220;consolidate his power further by making changes to the party apparatus,&#8221; influencing regulators in various sectors from finance to trade and cybersecurity.</p><p><img class="wp-image-15288 size-large aligncenter" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg" alt="" width="600" height="360" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min.jpg 1000w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /><noscript><img class="wp-image-15288 size-large aligncenter" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg" alt="" width="600" height="360" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/xijinpingplates-min.jpg 1000w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /></noscript></p><p>Posting the 9-page list of a total of 100 terms on Weibo, <em>People&#8217;s Daily</em> (@<a href="https://www.weibo.com/rmrb?refer_flag=1001030103_" target="_blank" rel="noopener">人民日报</a>) writes:</p><p style="text-align: left; padding-left: 30px;"><span style="color: #333333;"><em>&#8220;Study time! We want to teach you the translation of 100 hot terms for the 19th CPC National Congress (..) Do you know how to say these things in English? This is how to avoid using Chinglish and to express [these terms] in a more authentic way. They are all useful for CET-4 &amp; CET-6 [national English level tests in China] and other exams. Let&#8217;s learn these!&#8221; </em></span></p><p>By October 18, the list was shared 19000 times on Weibo and received many comments.</p><p>One <a href="https://www.weibo.com/2803301701/FqrkBdxID?refer_flag=1001030106_&amp;type=comment#_rnd1508259497740" target="_blank" rel="noopener">netizen</a> said: &#8220;With these 100 words you can understand a new China.&#8221; Others complained that they still think the English translation of these Chinese terms &#8220;sounds like Chinglish.&#8221;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4>Relevant Words: Policy Trends &amp; Digital Focus</h4><p>&nbsp;</p><p>The vocabulary list, which was selected from <em>China Daily</em>&#8216;s &#8220;Little Red Book of Hot Words&#8221; (热词红宝书), is an interesting combination of terms that says a lot about the focal points of the National Congress and the trends that are emphasized for the coming five years.</p><p>In the recent <a href="http://www.apcoworldwide.com/blog/detail/apcoforum/2017/10/16/chinas-19th-party-congress" target="_blank" rel="noopener">APCO report</a>, Gary Li mentions <strong>Ideological Tightening</strong> as a crucial policy trend. This promotion of &#8220;Chinese values&#8221; is clearly visible in the vocabularly list, that includes terms such as &#8220;the Chinese Dream&#8221; (中国梦), &#8220;Stay true to the mission&#8221; (不忘初心), and &#8220;cultural confidence&#8221; (文化自信).</p><p>Another important policy trend on the government agenda is <strong>Anti-Corruption</strong>, which is represented by the term &#8220;anti-corruption TV series&#8221; (反腐剧).</p><p>The list also includes some Internet slang terms such as &#8220;give a like&#8221; (点赞) or &#8220;phubber&#8221;/&#8221;<a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/bowed-head-clan-%E4%BD%8E%E5%A4%B4%E6%97%8F-mother-watched-phone-son-drowned/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">bowed head clan</a>&#8221; (低头族), referring to people who constantly look down to their smartphone.</p><p>It also includes a catchphrase that became especially popular on Chinese social media in 2016 when it was used by Chinese swimming champion <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wow-im-fast-olympic-swimmer-fu-yuanhui-becomes-chinese-internet-sensation/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Fu Yuanhui</a> during an interview about her winning medal during the Olympics &#8211; (&#8220;用了洪荒之力&#8221;), which can be translated as &#8220;I&#8217;ve used my primeval powers!&#8221;, basically meaning &#8220;to give one&#8217;s full play.&#8221;</p><div id="attachment_15311" style="width: 607px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img class="wp-image-15311 size-large" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-597x360.jpg" alt="" width="597" height="360" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-597x360.jpg 597w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-300x181.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui.jpg 600w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 597px) 100vw, 597px" /><noscript><img class="wp-image-15311 size-large" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-597x360.jpg" alt="" width="597" height="360" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-597x360.jpg 597w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-300x181.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/fuyuanhui.jpg 600w" sizes="(max-width: 597px) 100vw, 597px" /></noscript><p class="wp-caption-text">Swimmer Fu Yuanhui went viral in 2016 when she introduced a new catchphrase that is still a hot online sentence.</p></div><p>The inclusion of some typical internet catchphrases is especially noteworthy because in 2014, Chinese state media <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinese-government-says-no-to-internet-slang/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">published </a>that programs and commercials should not use Internet language to preserve traditional expressions.</p><p>The entire list has a clear<strong> Digital Focus</strong> when it comes to different industries, including government, media, finance, and traveling, introducing words such as &#8220;in-flight Wifi services&#8221; (空中上网服务), &#8220;face scan payment&#8221; (扫脸支付), 5G era (5G时代), and taxi-hailing app (打车软件).</p><div id="attachment_11300" style="width: 510px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img class="size-full wp-image-11300" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/thebeltandroadishow.jpg" alt="" width="500" height="350" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/thebeltandroadishow.jpg 500w, data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" /><noscript><img class="size-full wp-image-11300" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/thebeltandroadishow.jpg" alt="" sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" /></noscript><p class="wp-caption-text">The Belt and Road initiative and China&#8217;s role in the world is an important point on this year&#8217;s agenda.</p></div><p>The list also includes words that emphasize the <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-belt-road-propaganda-machine-runs-full-speed-overview/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Belt and Road Initiative</a> and <strong>China-centric Relations for Economy and Trade</strong>, such as the &#8220;New type of major-power relationship&#8221; (新型大国关系).</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4>The List: 100 Hot Words for the 19th National Congress</h4><p>&nbsp;</p><p>This is the full list of the 100 terms as shared by the <em>People&#8217;s Daily</em> through screenshots, typed out by What&#8217;s on Weibo. The pinyin and tones are also provided by What&#8217;s on Weibo.</p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15315" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/peoples-daily.jpg 600w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 404px) 100vw, 404px" /><noscript><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15315" https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/peoples-daily.jpg 600w" sizes="(max-width: 404px) 100vw, 404px" /></noscript></p><p>1. 中国梦<br /> <em>Zhōngguó mèng</em><br /> China dream</p><p>2. 不忘初心<br /> <em>Bù wàng chūxīn</em><br /> Stay true to the mission</p><p>3. 两个一百年<br /> <em>Liǎng gè yībǎi nián</em><br /> Two centenary goals</p><p>4. 新常态<br /> <em>Xīn chángtài</em><br /> New normal</p><p>5. 中国制造2025<br /> <em>Zhōngguó zhìzào 2025</em><br /> Made in China 2025</p><p>6. &#8220;双一流&#8221;<br /> <em>Shuāng yīliú</em><br /> Double First-Class initiative</p><p>7. 工匠精神<br /> <em>Gōngjiàng jīngshén</em><br /> Craftsmanship spirit</p><p>8. 中国天眼：500米口径球面射电望远镜(FAST)<br /> <em>Zhōngguó tiānyǎn:500 Mǐ kǒujìng qiúmiàn shèdiàn wàngyuǎnjìng (FAST)</em><br /> China’s Eye of Heaven: The 500-meter Aperture Spherical Telescope</p><p>9. 歼-20战斗机<br /> <em>Jiān-20 zhàndòujī</em><br /> J-20 Stealth Fighter</p><p>10. 国产航母<br /> <em>Guóchǎn hángmǔ</em><br /> Domestically built 量子卫星&#8221;墨子号&#8221;<br /> <em>Liàngzǐ wèixīng “mò </em>zi<em> hào”</em><br /> Quantum satellite &#8220;Micius&#8221;</p><p>14. 北斗卫星导航系统<br /> <em>Běidǒu wèixīng dǎoháng xìtǒng</em><br /> Beidou navigation system</p><p>15. 风云四号A星卫星<br /> <em>Fēngyún sì hào A xīng wèixīng</em><br /> Fengyun-4A satellite</p><p>16. 重型运载火箭<br /> <em>Zhòngxíng yùnzài huǒjiàn</em><br /> Heavy-lift Carrier <em>Jīng jīn jì yītǐ huà</em><br /> Beijing-Tianjin-Hebei integration</p><p>20. 雄安新区<br /> <em>Xióng ān xīnqū</em><br /> Xiong&#8217;an New Area</p><p>21. 自贸实验区<br /> <em>Zì mào shíyàn qū</em><br /> avatar-default" /></noscript></div><div class="mvp-author-info-text left relative"><div class="mvp-author-info-date left relative"><p>Published</p> <span class="mvp-post-date">2 days ago</span><p>on</p> <span class="mvp-post-date">October 26, 2017</span></div><div class="mvp-author-info-name left relative"><p>By</p> <span class="author-name"><a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/author/manya-koetse/" title="Posts by Manya Koetse" rel="author">Manya Koetse</a></span> <a href="" class="mvp-twit-but" target="_blank"><span class="mvp-author-info-twit-but"><i class="fa fa-twitter fa-2"></i></span></a></div></div></div></div><div class="mvp-post-add-body left relative"><div class="mvp-post-add-img left relative"> <img width="1000" height="600" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo.jpg" class="attachment- size- wp-post-image" alt="" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo.jpg 1000w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-400x240.jpg 400w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /><noscript><img width="1000" height="600" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo.jpg" class="attachment- size- wp-post-image" alt="" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo.jpg 1000w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/post90swhatsonweibo-400x240.jpg 400w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /></noscript></div><div class="mvp-post-add-cont left relative"><div class="mvp-post-add-main right relative"><div id="tps_slideContainer_13223" class="theiaPostSlider_slides"><div class="theiaPostSlider_preloadedSlide"><p><span class="myintro">Often considered lazy or fickle, China&#8217;s post-90s generation has a bad reputation when it comes to the workplace in China. But there is more than meets the eye. Upon entering the job market, the so-called <em>jiulinghou</em> workers are facing challenges that leave them either job-hopping or dog-tired.</span></p><p><span class="big">&#8216;L</span>azy&#8217;, &#8216;spoilt&#8217;, &#8216;pampered&#8217;, and &#8216;selfish&#8217; &#8211; just some of the words that surface when you ask many Chinese people about the country&#8217;s &#8216;<em>jiulinghou</em>&#8216; (九零後), a term that is commonly used to describe those born into China&#8217;s new urban middle-class families between 1990 and 1999.</p><p>The generational differences between those born after 1970, 1980, and the Chinese born after 1990 have been a topic of discussion on social media for years. The generation gap seems to be especially apparent when it comes to views on work and career, and attitudes in the workplace.</p><p>One Weibo netizen recently <a href="http://www.weibo.com/u/3600991542?refer_flag=1001030103_" target="_blank" rel="noopener">wrote</a>: &#8220;I have a new colleague who was born in the 1990s. The other day, she requested a leave of absence. We asked her what she was going to do. She said &#8216;I&#8217;m just going to get some plastic surgery done, but I&#8217;ll be back soon.'&#8221;</p><p>Last year, one recently graduated male real estate agent <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-post-1990s-job-hopping-generation/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">made the news</a> when he quit his job because there were &#8220;too many women in the workplace&#8221;, which &#8220;negatively influenced&#8221; his personality. His resignation letter went viral shortly after.</p><div id="attachment_5585" style="width: 510px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img class="wp-image-5585 size-full" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign.jpg" alt="" width="500" height="336" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign.jpg 500w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign-300x202.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign-230x155.jpg 230w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" /><noscript><img class="wp-image-5585 size-full" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign.jpg" alt="" width="500" height="336" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign.jpg 500w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign-300x202.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/resign-230x155.jpg 230w" sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" /></noscript><p class="wp-caption-text">A post-90s resignation letter went viral on Weibo.</p></div><p>Another resignation that <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-post-1990s-job-hopping-generation/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">made its rounds</a> on social media was that of a Hunan female office worker who wrote her employer that she was quitting her job because &#8220;winter is too cold&#8221;, making it &#8220;difficult to get out of bed in the morning.&#8221;</p><p>The post-90s generation is often considered to be fickle and self-focused in their work. They are generally viewed as bad team players who are much less concerned about hierarchical relations at the workplace than China’s older generations are.</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4><strong>NOT ALL ABOUT THE MONEY</strong></h4><blockquote><p><em><span style="font-size: 35px;">&#8220;There&#8217;s a big gap between what we imagined our work to be and what the reality is.&#8221;</span></em></p></blockquote><p>&nbsp;</p><p>Are China&#8217;s post-90s really that lazy and picky, or are they just tired? According to the song &#8220;I&#8217;m Dog-Tired&#8221; by the Shanghai Rainbow Chamber Singers, it is the latter. The song became <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/im-dog-tired-viral-choir-song-resonates-stressed-young-chinese/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">an instant hit</a> last year, as it resonated with China&#8217;s young professionals who recognized themselves in the lyrics.</p><p>The song describes the monolog of person who is caught up in overwork all the time, saying: &#8220;<em>I haven’t washed my face for 18 days / I’ve been wearing my 30-day contact lenses for 2,5 years now</em>.&#8221;</p><div id="attachment_15514" style="width: 550px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-540x360.jpg" alt="" width="540" height="360" class="size-large wp-image-15514" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-540x360.jpg 540w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-300x200.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401.jpg 600w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 540px) 100vw, 540px" /><noscript><img src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-540x360.jpg" alt="" width="540" height="360" class="size-large wp-image-15514" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-540x360.jpg 540w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401-300x200.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/f04da2db14841903e65401.jpg 600w" sizes="(max-width: 540px) 100vw, 540px" /></noscript><p class="wp-caption-text">This Shanghai choir of young professionals scored a hit by voicing their dissatisfaction about working overtime.</p></div><p>But it is not just their everyday work that tires out the young Chinese working population, it&#8217;s also the job-hopping they do. According to research by the <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-post-1990s-job-hopping-generation/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Mycos Institute</a>, only 40% of China&#8217;s post-90s workers stay in their job for longer than two years. Within a time frame of three years, 8% has four or more different jobs.</p><p>What is the main problem of the post-90 workers that leads to <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-post-1990s-job-hopping-generation/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">all this job-hopping</a> and sleepless nights? Is the pressure on China&#8217;s job market too much to handle for this only-child generation?</p><p>&#8220;The biggest obstacle to overcome for me and most of my friends is the fact that there&#8217;s a big gap between what we imagined our work to be and what the reality is,&#8221; Yue Xin tells What&#8217;s on Weibo. Yue did her Bachelor&#8217;s at a Shanghai college and recently completed a master&#8217;s degree in liberal arts at a British university.</p><p>&#8220;I read on Weibo the other day that, unlike the post-70s and post-80s generation, China&#8217;s young job-seekers prioritize personal happiness and freedom over anything else,&#8221; she says: &#8220;For many of us, a long-term contract does not feel like a reassurance but like a constraint, which might prevent us from taking on more exciting challenges. It is not all about the money &#8211; it is about following our passion.&#8221;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4><strong>CHINA&#8217;S PRICELESS CHILDREN</strong></h4><blockquote><p><em><span style="font-size: 35px;">&#8220;Around 8 million university graduates enter China&#8217;s job market each year.&#8221;</span></em></p></blockquote><p>&nbsp;</p><p>The high job expectations among China&#8217;s post-90s workers relate to their position in their families and in society at large. As described by Liu Fengshu (2015) in &#8220;The Rise of the &#8216;Priceless&#8217; Child in China,&#8221; the so-called <em>jiulinghou</em> is a one-child generation that was born amidst the rapid socio-economic changes of post-Mao China, which saw a dramatic growth of both wealth and technological developments.</p><p>Parents and grandparents have both pampered and pressured these children; not just because it takes more than a high school education to succeed in a society that is changing so quickly, but also because the urban post-90s generation was the first to have access to education and career opportunities in a way their (grand)parents never had. They are therefore also often called the &#8216;lucky generation&#8217; (幸运的一代).</p><div id="attachment_15480" style="width: 460px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img class="size-full wp-image-15480" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad.jpg" alt="" width="450" height="290" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad.jpg 450w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad-300x193.jpg 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px" /><noscript><img class="size-full wp-image-15480" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad.jpg" alt="" width="450" height="290" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad.jpg 450w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/s4_5462f2c280cad-300x193.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px" /></noscript><p class="wp-caption-text">Editorial cartoon from Chinese media. Left is the post-70s who says |I have to work overtime.&#8221; In the middle the post-80s generation saying: &#8220;I won&#8217;t work overtime.&#8221; On the right the post-90 generation saying: &#8220;I won&#8217;t work at all.&#8221;</p></div><p>But all this parental investment has also set the bar high for the future. Around 8 million new university graduates now enter China&#8217;s job market each year, but their chances of finding a job that suits their education and personal expectations are slim.</p><p>With all their high hopes and graduate diplomas, they are facing a job market mismatch. They often have no working experience and, as they have often spent years studying before entering the employment market, they are not willing to take on jobs with low education requirements.</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4><strong>&#8216;LUCKY&#8217; BUT STRESSED</strong></h4><blockquote><p><span style="font-size: 35px;"><em>&#8220;If any of these requirements are not there, it will be very stressful for us.&#8221;</em></span></p></blockquote><p>&nbsp;</p><p>Is the <em>jiulinghou</em> being unreasonable in what they expect from their work? A Beijing post-90er nicknamed &#8216;Pedy&#8217;, who teaches Chinese to foreigners at a Chaoyang educational institution, does not think so. She tells What&#8217;s on Weibo: &#8220;We all just want a job that (1) we find interesting, (2) suits our skills, (3) offers a reasonable salary, (4) is located not too far from where we live, and (5) gives us a sense of success or achievement. If any of these requirements are not there, it will be very stressful for us.&#8221;</p><p>&#8216;Pedy&#8217; mentions the cost of life in China&#8217;s bigger cities as one of the major problems: &#8220;The salaries of people just starting out on the job market are generally quite low, while the cost of living in cities like Beijing is very high. But if you live too far from your company, it means spending long and tiring hours crammed in public transport every morning and every evening.&#8221;</p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15485" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-600x360.jpg" alt="" width="600" height="360" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min.jpg 1000w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /><noscript><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15485" src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-600x360.jpg" alt="" width="600" height="360" srcset="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/commutingpost90swhatsonweibo-min.jpg 1000w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /></noscript></p><p>Because so many people do not find a job that meets their requirements, they either choose to remain jobless for some time to explore their possibilities, or to hop from company to company until they find what they are looking for. Unafraid of losing a job they do not care much for anyway, many of these post-90ers are those who have become known for quitting their job because of the &#8216;cold weather&#8217; or other seemingly random reasons.</p><p>&nbsp;</p><h4><strong>THE SO-CALLED &#8216;DREAM JOB&#8217;</strong></h4><blockquote><p><em><span style="font-size: 35px;">&#8220;If we do not finish our projects in time, they will subtract an amount from our wages.&#8221;</span></em></p></blockquote><p>&nbsp;</p><p>Perhaps the biggest challenge faced by China&#8217;s well-educated, urban post-90s workers who are entering the employment market is the troubling Catch 22 situation at hand: they will be stressed and pressured if they do not find that top job, but when they do, they are often also stressed and pressured.</p><p>When scoring a much-desired job at one of the top companies (such as one of the &#8216;Big Four&#8217; firms Deloitte, Ernst &#038; Young, PricewaterhouseCoopers/PwC and KPMG), young workers will often do all they can to keep their job. These jobs come with relatively high salaries and future possibilities to higher positions, but they also go hand in hand with long hours and unpaid overwork. Those who refuse to work overtime will be labeled as &#8216;non-ambitious&#8217; or &#8216;not loyal enough.&#8217;</p><p>Beijing resident Li Jiang has a good job that suits his skills, is not too far from home, has a good salary, and offers prospects for further growth. Despite his stable contract, he is used to working over hours and often does not come home until late at night.</p><p>&#8220;We do not get paid for overtime,&#8221; Li says: &#8220;But they just give us too much work to handle. If we do not finish our projects in time, they will subtract an amount from our wages, although this is not noted in my contract.&#8221;</p><p>Although (illegal) overtime may endanger workers&#8217; health due to the excessive long working hours, it is still commonplace in China (Kim &#038; Chung 2016). Over recent years, some stories of young professionals literally working themselves to death &#8211; also known by the Japanese term &#8216;karoshi&#8217; &#8211; have made headlines.</p><p>In 2011, the story of the 25-year-old PwC auditor Pan Jie <a href="http://shanghaiist.com/2011/04/15/25-year-old_shanghai_auditor_worked_to_death.php" rel="noopener" target="_blank">went viral</a> on Sina Weibo when doctors <a href="http://ascportfolios.org/chinaandmedia/2011/04/13/a-auditor-lady-in-pwc-died-from-overwork/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">concluded</a> that her overwork at the company might have played a crucial role in her death.</p><p>Likewise, the behind-the-desk death of a <a href="http://adage.com/article/global-news/young-ogilvy-china-staffer-s-death-raises-issue-overwork/241500/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">24-year-old Ogilvy employee </a>in Beijing and the <a href="http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/china/2016-06/30/content_25920247.htm" rel="noopener" target="_blank">2016 death of Jin Bo</a>, a deputy editor-in-chief of one of China&#8217;s leading online forums, all prompted calls for increased public awareness on the risks of overwork &#8211; especially amongs young professionals.</p><p>Despite these headlines, Li continues working over hours: &#8220;Perhaps it&#8217;s in our culture. Nobody wants to be the one leaving first or sticking their heads out to ask about employee rights. <em>Meiyoubanfa</em>, it&#8217;s just the way it is.&#8221;</p><p>Yue Xin from Shanghai has something different in mind for her future. She has received job offers from several companies, but despite &#8220;feeling flattered,&#8221; none of them met her expectations. She is not lazy or fickle, she says; she is currently just looking for more interesting opportunities and is &#8220;following her passions&#8221; in Europe.</p><p><em>By <a href="http://www.twitter.com/manyapan" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Manya Koetse</a></em><br /> <a class="twitter-follow-button" href="https://twitter.com/whatsonweibo" data-show-count="false">Follow @whatsonweibo</a><script async src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script></p><p>References</p><p>Fengshu Liu. 2016. &#8220;The Rise of the “Priceless” Child in China.&#8221; <em>Comparative Education Review</em> 60 (1): 105-130.</p><p>Kim, S., &#038; Chung, S. 2016. &#8220;Explaining Organizational Responsiveness to Emerging Regulatory Pressure: The Case of Illegal Overtime in China.&#8221; <em>The International Journal of Human Resource Management</em> 27(18): 2097–2118.</p><p><em>Spotted a mistake or want to add something? rel="bookmark"><span class="mvp-post-add-link-but">Continue Reading</span></a></div></div></div></div><div class="mvp-post-add-story left relative"><div class="mvp-post-add-head left relative"><h3 class="mvp-post-cat left relative"><a class="mvp-post-cat-link" href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/category/chinainsight/"><span class="mvp-post-cat left">China Insight</span></a></h3><h1 class="mvp-post-title left">&#8220;What&#8217;s Modernisation?&#8221; &#8211; Chinese State Media Explain China&#8217;s &#8216;New Era&#8217; With a Rap Video</h1> <span class="mvp-post-excerpt left"><p>No three-and-a-half-hour speech, but a three-and-a-half minute video explains China&#8217;s new strategies in this latest propaganda clip on social media.</p> </span><div class="mvp-author-info-wrap left relative"><div class="mvp-author-info-thumb left relative"> <img src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/alicemingay-50x50.jpg" width="46" height="46" alt="Alice Mingay" class="avatar avatar-46 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-46 alignnone photo" /><noscript><img src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/alicemingay-50x50.jpg" width="46" height="46" alt="Alice Mingay" class="avatar avatar-46 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-46 alignnone photo" /></noscript></div><div class="mvp-author-info-text left relative"><div class="mvp-author-info-date left relative"><p>Published</p> <span class="mvp-post-date">7 days ago</span><p>on</p> <span class="mvp-post-date">October 20, 2017</span></div><div class="mvp-author-info-name left relative"><p>By</p> <span class="author-name"><a 400w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /></noscript></div><div class="mvp-post-add-cont left relative"><div class="mvp-post-add-main right relative"><div id="tps_slideContainer_15377" class="theiaPostSlider_slides"><div class="theiaPostSlider_preloadedSlide"><p><span class="myintro">No three-and-a-half-hour speech, but a three-and-a-half minute video &#8211; Chinese state media explain China&#8217;s new strategies through catchy rap music and trendy graphics.</span></p><p><span class="big">T</span>he much-anticipated <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/100-terms-communist-party-wants-know-19th-cpc-national-congress/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">19th Party Congress</a> opened last Wednesday in Beijing with Xi Jinping&#8217;s three-and-a-half-hour speech on &#8220;Thoughts on Socialism with Chinese Characteristics for a New Era&#8221; (新时代中国特色社会主义思想), which presented the Party’s new concepts, thoughts and strategies &#8211; with Xi himself at its core.</p><p><em>Shi-jiu-da</em> (十九大, &#8216;big 19&#8217;) is the popular abbreviation for the 19th Congress of the Communist Party of China. This Plenum is held once every five years and is the highest level political meeting in the Chinese calendar. The meeting is also a big topic on Chinese social media; the Weibo hashtag for the &#8216;big 19&#8217; event #<a href="https://www.weibo.com/p/1008085f88278c703c75008dcc372ed7e72216?k=%25E5%258D%2581%25E4%25B9%259D%25E5%25A4%25A7&amp;from=526&amp;_from_=huati_topic" target="_blank" rel="noopener">十九大</a># was viewed over 3,6 billion times on Friday.</p><p>As with previous major political gatherings, speeches and rhetoric are not the only means by which the Party and state media seek to convey their message to the wider population. A video titled &#8220;What is modernization? Let us tell you in a rap!&#8221; (“现代化”是什么化？一段嘻哈告诉你!) is the latest in a series produced by state broadcaster CCTV. The video is being spread through social media.</p><p>The clip (<em><a href="https://m.weibo.cn/status/4163242974762288?luicode=20000061&amp;lfid=4163242974762288&amp;wm=3333_2001&amp;retcode=6102" target="_blank" rel="noopener">click link</a> or see embedded video below</em>), that lays out the government&#8217;s stategies for China&#8217;s &#8216;new era&#8217; through rap music with bright graphics, was widely distributed on Chinese social media this week by various media platforms and institutions, from the <em>Economic Observer</em> (@<a href="https://www.weibo.com/eeocomcn?refer_flag=1001030103_&amp;is_hot=1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">经济观察报</a>) to the Ministry of Public Security.</p><p><iframe src="about:blank" data-lazy-src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/CfsoPTStUfI?rel=0" width="560" height="315" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen"></iframe></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;">The translation of the video&#8217;s full text* is as follows:</p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Let’s go!</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">This October in Beijing</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">&#8230;will all be arriving!</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">The time has come for 十九大（shi-jiu-da）</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Listen out for the important voices</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">十九大 (shi-jiu-da) let’s say a little about it</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">There is a lot of information here</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">So, listen out carefully and I’ll speak slowly</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">In the past, China has always advanced courageously</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">As we have said before,</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">When difficult problems are solved then great things can be established!</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Our nation is full of vigor and vitality!</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15401" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/dahu-617x360.jpg" alt="" width="617" height="360" https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/dahu.jpg 812w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 617px) 100vw, 617px" /><noscript><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15401" /></noscript></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Anti-corruption efforts are strong</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Many tigers have been taken down</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">From rocket lift-offs to submarine exercises,</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Technology is changing our lives</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Haha, Haha, Haha,</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">As I’m going to show up next, we have plans going forward…</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15396" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" voice speaking:]</strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"> <em><span style="color: #333333;">By the time we reach the middle period of this century, we will have built a modern socialist state which is rich and powerful, democratic, civilised, and harmonious. In this way, we will have realized the great rejuvenation of the Chinese people.</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #333333;">[Rap continues:]</span></strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">But, building in accordance with the needs of modernization</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">What even is modernization?</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Let me tell you:</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large 617px" /></noscript></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>[End of rap, start of explanation by lecturer:]</strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"> <em><span style="color: #333333;">100 years ago, Sun Yat-sen set out a blueprint for modernization in ‘Strategy for Building a Nation’: b</span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">uild train tracks, repair the roads, construct large ports. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">At that time, this was still considered fantastical and unrealistic.</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">But today, train lines criss-cross the whole nation! </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">They run N-S between Beijing-Guangdong-Shanghai, as well as across the well-trodden route of Lanzhou-Chengdu-Chongqing. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">The length of the journey on the bullet trains just keeps reducing!</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Again, at the time the People’s Republic was founded, n</span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">ot even a tractor could be built! </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">Thus, building a modern, industrial socialist nation became our aim.</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15395" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" data-lazy-src="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/modernisationchina2-617x360.jpg" alt="" width="617" #333333;">In 1954, the first National People’s Congress was held.  </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">This was the first time the aim of achieving the Four Modernizations was clearly referenced. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">In just the next few years, factory after factory was built, including those of Anshan Steel works and Changchun car manufacturers.</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Our workers are powerful!</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15397" /></noscript></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">This was a song I would listen to when I was young, and hearing it I would know my dad would soon finish work for the day and so I would quickly pack away all my marbles. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">Entering the period of opening and reform, Deng Xiaoping named the Four Modernizations as the way to ‘Chinese Modernization’, as well as wanting to become a middle-income nation.</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">In the 1970s, when people married, the three major durable consumer goods were still watches, bicycles and sewing machines. In the 80s, this became fridges, </span>color TVs<span style="color: #333333;">, and washing machines, and by the 90s changed again into air conditioning, cameras, and camcorders.</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="color: #333333;">[Xi Jinping’s voice:]</span></strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Now, information technologies such as the internet are changing with each passing day. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">This is leading a new revolution in </span>society</em> <em><span style="color: #333333;">and bringing new dimensions into human lives.</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15405" #333333;">[Presenter continues:]</span></strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">A report from the 18th Party Congress, published on 8th November 2012, mentioned the ‘4 New Modernisations.’ </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">This has led to the implementation of an innovation-driven development strategy. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">Over the last 5 years, the major technological developments we have made have accumulated further and further. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">The computing in the Sunway Taihu Light is the most advanced in the world.</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">The quantum satellite Mozi Hao is unparalleled. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">The Tiangong 2 satellite has been sent off smoothly. </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">Each of these </span>wondrous<span style="color: #333333;"> engineering projects is a feat of its own! </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">What a country!</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">In 2013, General Secretary Xi Jinping then added one more </span>modernization<span style="color: #333333;"> into the fold, that being to </span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">‘continue to advance the nation’s governing system, and to </span>modernize<span style="color: #333333;"> our governing capabilities.’</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Modernisation as a whole is very impressive. Frankly speaking, only this </span>modernization<span style="color: #333333;"> of the inner qualities of officials and</span></em> <em>organizations<span style="color: #333333;"> will enable them to govern the country and change the civilized norms.</span></em><em><span style="color: #333333;">We don’t take a break from modernization!</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>[Rap continues:]</strong></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">Yeah, now that we have become a middle-class society</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">We have reached the most important section of our reform agenda</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">What are the issues that affect the lives of the middle class?</span></em></p><p style="padding-left: 30px;"><em><span style="color: #333333;">At this stage in the development of Socialism with Chinese Characteristics,</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">People are heading in the direction of a better life</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">The Party must remember</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">This is a new beginning!</span></em></p><p><img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-15399" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP///wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=" #333333;">In what direction is the bullet train heading?</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">After 200 years, will the Chinese dream have been </span>realized<span style="color: #333333;">?</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">What expectations do Chinese families have for their future?</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Will the 十九大 (shi-jiu-da) </span>answer<span style="color: #333333;"> these questions for you?</span></em><br /> <em><span style="color: #333333;">Of course!</span></em></p><p>Both the design and the genre of the new clip show some resemblance to clips launched during the <a href="https://www.whatsonweibo.com/chinas-belt-road-propaganda-machine-runs-full-speed-overview/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Belt and Road Summit</a> earlier this year.</p><p>On Weibo, a platform that is heavily controlled during the 19th National Congress, the video was shared hundreds of times. Although discussions on the video are limited due to current restrictions, one surprised netizen just posted: &#8220;Can I actually comment on this?!&#8221;</p><p><em>By Alice Mingay</em><br /> <a class="twitter-follow-button" href="https://twitter.com/whatsonweibo" data-show-count="false">Follow @whatsonweibo</a><script async src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script></p><p>* Full Text:<br /> Let’s go!<br /> 在十月里的北京<br /> 。。。。都到这里 （3-4）<br /> 十九大要来了<br /> 听听到重要的声音<br /> 十九大，说点嘛？</p><p>这里信息有点多<br /> 你听我慢慢说<br /> 过去砥砺奋进<br /> 也我们互相说过<br /> 难提解决大事办成<br /> 祖国朝气蓬勃<br /> 反腐力度很大<br /> 打掉的老虎很多<br /> 胖五升空，蛟龙下水<br /> 科技改变生活<br /> 哈哈，哈哈，哈哈<br /> 接下来，我们还有个目标</p><p>[习近平的声音：]<br /> 到本世纪中叶建成富强民主<br /> 文明和谐的社会主义现代化国家，<br /> 实现中华民族伟大复兴。<br /> &#8211;中共中烟总书记、国家主席、中央军委主席习近平</p><p>建设现代化<br /> 那现代化是什么？<br /> 来，听我跟你说<br /> 百年前，孙中山在[建国方略]里描绘了现代化的蓝图<br /> 建铁路、修公路、建造水平大海港<br /> 这些的当时，还被认为是‘空想’<br /> 而如今，京广、京沪穿南北<br /> 兰渝铁路通蜀道<br /> 复兴号路途时间再修短</p><p>再说，新中国刚成立时<br /> 一台拖拉机都不能造<br /> 建成社会主义现代化工业国就是我们的目标</p><p>1954年，第一届全国人民代表大会<br /> 第一次明确提出要实现四个现代化<br /> 随后的几年里，鞍山无缝钢管厂、长春第一汽车制造厂一个厂接一个厂<br /> 咱们工人有力量</p><p>‘咱们工人有力量’<br /> 小时候一听到这首歌就知道爸爸要下班了，赶紧把玻璃球收起来<br /> 迈入改革开放新时期，邓小平把实现四个现代化的目标称为‘中国式的现代化’，也就是‘小康之家’。<br /> 70年代，人们结婚， ‘三大件’还是手表自行车缝纫机<br /> 80年代，冰箱、彩电、洗衣机<br /> 90年代变成空调、音像、录像机</p><p>现在以互联网为代表的信息技术日新月异<br /> 引领了社会生产新变革<br /> 创造了人类生活新空间</p><p>2012年11月8号的中共十八大报告提出了 ‘新四化’<br /> 实施创新驱动发展战略<br /> 这五年，祖国的科技发展硕果累累<br /> 超级计算机“神威-太湖之光”世界第一<br /> 量子卫星‘墨子号’世界独一无二<br /> ‘天宫二号’顺利发射<br /> 奇迹工程一个个，厉害了，我的国</p><p>2013年习近平总书记又给这新四化加了一化<br /> 不断推进国家治理体系和治理能力现代化</p><p>整个现代化，有点厉害了<br /> 说白了，就是国家机构官员素质的现代化是治理国家变得文明规范<br /> 建设现代化，我们不放假</p><p>Yeah, 如今全面建成小康社会<br /> 到最关键的议程<br /> 小康心内还是什么事关你我的生活<br /> 中国特色社会主义进行的发展阶段<br /> 人民群众向往的美好生活<br /> 党中要记得<br /> 这是一个新的起点<br /> 复兴号驶向哪儿？<br /> 两个一百年后，中国梦实现了吗？<br /> 对于祖国家庭未来，还有那些期待？<br /> 来过这十九大，还为你来解答？<br /> 必须的</p><p>Edited by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/manyapan"><em>Manya Koetse</em></a><br /> <em>Spotted a mistake or want to add something? 	var logoHeight = $("#mvp-main-nav-top").outerHeight();
	var botHeight = $("#mvp-main-nav-bot").outerHeight();
	var navHeight = $("#mvp-main-head-wrap").outerHeight();

				$("#mvp-main-nav-top").addClass("mvp-fixed");
				$("#mvp-main-nav-bot").addClass("mvp-fixed1");
				$("#mvp-main-body-wrap").css("margin-top", totalHeight );
				$("#mvp-main-nav-top").addClass("mvp-fixed-shadow");
				$(".mvp-nav-top-mid").addClass("mvp-fixed-post");
				$(".mvp-drop-nav-title").show();
				$(".mvp-fly-top").addClass("mvp-to-top");
	    		if(scroll < previousScroll) {
					$("#mvp-main-nav-bot").addClass("mvp-fixed2");
					$("#mvp-main-nav-top").removeClass("mvp-fixed-shadow");
					$("#mvp-main-nav-top").removeClass("mvp-soc-mob-up");
					$("#mvp-soc-mob-wrap").removeClass("mvp-soc-mob-up");
				} else {
					$("#mvp-main-nav-bot").removeClass("mvp-fixed2");
					$("#mvp-main-nav-top").addClass("mvp-fixed-shadow");
					$("#mvp-main-nav-top").addClass("mvp-soc-mob-up");
					$("#mvp-soc-mob-wrap").addClass("mvp-soc-mob-up");
				}
			} else {
				$("#mvp-main-nav-top").removeClass("mvp-fixed");
				$("#mvp-main-nav-bot").removeClass("mvp-fixed1");
				$("#mvp-main-nav-bot").removeClass("mvp-fixed2");
				$("#mvp-main-body-wrap").css("margin-top","0");
				$("#mvp-main-nav-top").removeClass("mvp-fixed-shadow");
				$(".mvp-nav-top-mid").removeClass("mvp-fixed-post");
				$(".mvp-drop-nav-title").hide();
	    		$(".mvp-fly-top").removeClass("mvp-to-top");
			}
			previousScroll = scroll;
	});
	});
	});
	

	jQuery(document).ready(function($) {
	// Video Post Scroll
	$(window).on("scroll.video", function(event){
		var scrollTop     = $(window).scrollTop();
    	var elementOffset = $("#mvp-content-wrap").offset().top;
    	var distance      = (elementOffset - scrollTop);
		var aboveHeight = $("#mvp-video-embed-wrap").outerHeight();
		if ($(window).scrollTop() > distance + aboveHeight + screen.height){
			$("#mvp-video-embed-cont").addClass("mvp-vid-fixed");
			$("#mvp-video-embed-wrap").addClass("mvp-vid-height");
			$(".mvp-video-close").show();
		} else {
			$("#mvp-video-embed-cont").removeClass("mvp-vid-fixed");
			$("#mvp-video-embed-wrap").removeClass("mvp-vid-height");
			$(".mvp-video-close").hide();
		}
	});

 	$(".mvp-video-close").on("click", function(){
		$("iframe").attr("src", $("iframe").attr("src"));
		$("#mvp-video-embed-cont").removeClass("mvp-vid-fixed");
		$("#mvp-video-embed-wrap").removeClass("mvp-vid-height");
		$(".mvp-video-close").hide();
		$(window).off("scroll.video");
  	});

	});

 		$(".mvp-soc-mob-right").on("click", function(){
			$("#mvp-soc-mob-wrap").toggleClass("mvp-soc-mob-more");
  		});
  	});
	});

    	  $(this).children("ul").toggle();
	  $(".mvp-fly-nav-menu").getNiceScroll().resize();
	  }
	  $(this).toggleClass("tog-minus");
    	  return false;
  	});

	// Main Menu Scroll
	$(window).load(function(){
	  $(".mvp-fly-nav-menu").niceScroll({cursorcolor:"#888",cursorwidth: 7,cursorborder: 0,zindex:999999});
	});
	});

    sessionStorage.setItem('h5ab-print-article', '<div id="h5ab-print-content"><h1>These are the 100 Terms the Communist Party Wants You to Know for the 19th CPC National Congress</h1>' + "<p><!-- BEGIN THEIA POST SLIDER --><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"myintro\">These are the 100 terms to know for the 19th CPC National Congress &#8211; propagated by <em>People&#8217;s Daily<\/em>, the mouthpiece of China&#8217;s ruling Communist Party, on Weibo.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"big\">I<\/span>t is the week of the 19th National Congress of the Communist Party of China (CPC), better known as the &#8220;19th Party Congress.&#8221; This meeting, that takes place from October 18 to October 24, is a major event that takes place every five years.<\/p>\n<p>On Chinese social media, Communist Party newspaper <em>People&#8217;s Daily<\/em> (@<a href=\"https:\/\/www.weibo.com\/rmrb?refer_flag=1001030103_\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u4eba\u6c11\u65e5\u62a5<\/a>) presented a vocabulary list for people to know before the huge political event.<\/p>\n<p>During the 19th Party Congress approximately 2280 delegates from across the nation officially come together to select the party\u2019s top leadership for the next five years. The event is <a href=\"http:\/\/www.aljazeera.com\/news\/2017\/10\/explained-national-congress-china-communist-party-171017140021234.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">also called<\/a> a &#8220;celebration of decisions that have already been taken,&#8221; as the key points of the meeting have mostly already been settled behind closed doors.<\/p>\n<p>It is these key decisions for China that will be discussed during the CPC National Congress and then officially announced, representing &#8220;new governance concepts, thoughts and strategies proposed by the CPC Central Committee with Xi Jinping at its core&#8221; influencing regulators in various sectors from finance to trade and cybersecurity.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"wp-image-15288 size-large aligncenter\" src=\"data:image\/gif;base64,R0lGODdhAQABAPAAAP\/\/\/wAAACwAAAAAAQABAEACAkQBADs=\" data-lazy-src=\"https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" data-lazy-srcset=\"https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min.jpg 1000w\" data-lazy-sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" \/><noscript><img class=\"wp-image-15288 size-large aligncenter\" src=\"https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" srcset=\"https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-600x360.jpg 600w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-300x180.jpg 300w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-590x354.jpg 590w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min-400x240.jpg 400w, https:\/\/www.whatsonweibo.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2017\/10\/xijinpingplates-min.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" \/><\/noscript><\/p>\n<p>Posting the 9-page list of a total of 100 terms on Weibo, <em>People&#8217;s Daily<\/em> (@<a href=\"https:\/\/www.weibo.com\/rmrb?refer_flag=1001030103_\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u4eba\u6c11\u65e5\u62a5<\/a>) writes:<\/p>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;     $.strRemove = function(theTarget, theString) {
        return $("<div/>").append(
            $(theTarget, theString).remove().end()
        ).html();
    };

    var articleStr = sessionStorage.getItem('h5ab-print-article');
    var removeArr = ['video','audio','script','iframe'];

    $.each(removeArr, function(index, value){
        var processedCode = $.strRemove(value, articleStr);
        articleStr = processedCode;
    });
    
    var fullPrintContent = articleStr;
    sessionStorage.setItem('h5ab-print-article', fullPrintContent);
